                        <a id="moneyMarketNote2">&nbsp;</a>	 					
<div id="disclosureMM" style="">
							<!-- check for Money Market Relatioship product to determine if the disclosure needs to be shown-->



	

	
		
	

	
		
	


<p class="disclosure">1. In order to qualify for a Relationship Rate on Premiere Money Market, you must have a linked checking account (for the Performance Checking Relationship Rate, you must have a linked Performance Checking or Virtual WalletÂ® with Performance Spend; for the Performance Select Checking Relationship Rate, you must have a linked Performance Select Checking or Virtual Wallet with Performance Select) and meet one of the following requirements:
</p>
<ul class="ulDisclosure noPadding">
	<li>â€¢	Make a combination of 5 or more PIN and/or signature point-of-sale transactions (excluding cash advances) posted during the previous calendar month to your Checking account using your VisaÂ® Debit Card or to your linked Visa Credit Card.</li>
	<li>â€¢	Have $2,000 in qualifying direct deposits ($1,000 for WorkPlace or Military Banking customers) in a linked Virtual Wallet with Performance Spend or Performance Checking during the previous calendar month.</li>
	<li>â€¢	Have $5,000 in qualifying direct deposits in a linked Virtual Wallet with Performance Select or Performance Select Checking during the previous calendar month.</li>
</ul>
<p class="disclosure">Starting with the calendar month following when you open your Premiere Money Market account and monthly thereafter, whether the account earns the variable Standard or Relationship Rate for the entire calendar month will be determined on the first of the month based upon the number of qualifying transactions or direct deposit requirement from the previous calendar month.
</p>
<p class="disclosure">If there are changes to your linked checking account (it is closed, changed to a new account type or no longer linked to your Premiere Money Market account), you may no longer qualify for a Relationship Rate, or the rates may otherwise change to those in effect at the time of the change.
</p>

In addition, your CD rate will convert to the rate applicable to the standard CD term.

Percentage Rate (APR) for all advances on all existing balances will be subject to change on the first day of each month based on the Basic Savings rate published monthly. For Credit Card Loans, the rate is based on your creditworthiness.  The APR will vary with the market based on the Prime Rate.   The maximum interest rate will never exceed the rate permitted under the Federal Credit Union Act (currently, this maximum is 18%).  If your rate increases, additional payments will be required.  For Overdraft Line-of-Credit (Checking Reserve), rates are subject to change.  Fixed Home Equity Loan rate reflects a 0.25% discount for direct deposit. Undergraduate Private Education Line-of-Credit Loan rate reflects a 0.25% discount for auto-pay during repayment only. Quorum is an equal housing lender.</div></div><div class="all-tables-wrap"><h2 class="tables-title" id="Banking" tabindex="0">Banking <span class="mobile-show" tabindex="0">Rates</span></h2><div <p>â€  Annual Percentage Yield(APY). APY calculation assumes that funds will be held on deposit for 365 days with no rate change, fees assessed, withdrawals, or deposits made and will be applied to the entire collected balance of the applicable tier.</p>
<p><sup>1</sup>The increased Annual Percentage Yield added to the Personal Money Market and/or Rewards CD base APY is valid only for the time the customer remains at the required Rewards Banking Level. If a customer falls into a lower Rewards Level that does not receive the increased APY (i.e., Silver Level), the customer's APY will revert to the normal Personal Money Market and/or Personal CD APY at that time. IRA CDs are NOT eligible for Rewards CD increased APYs. Customers may not combine promotional offers, rates, or other incentives with discounts or increases in the APY for Rewards Banking accounts.</p>
<p>Please refer to the <a href="/-/media/Files/Disclosures/DISC-MKT-020_combined.pdf?la=en&amp;hash=B36DE9B12FE5DD1F65EA93F4B2A5E38BC3ADB86D">Understanding Your Deposit Account Agreement &amp; Disclosures (UYDAAD)</a> brochure, Addendums to the UYDAAD, and the Schedule of Fees and Minimum Balances for additional information about the terms and conditions that apply to deposit accounts and services. CD accounts earn interest at a fixed rate, except for Rewards CDs, which earn interest at a variable rate. Fixed rate means that, after the CD is opened, you receive the applicable interest rate until the CD matures. The checking, savings, and money market accounts listed above are variable rate accounts. Variable rate means that at our discretion, we may change the Annual Percentage Yield/Interest Rate on the account at any time.</p>
<p><strong>Rewards CDs, Personal CDs, CESA CDs, IRA CDs:</strong>&nbsp;There is no minimum balance to obtain the disclosed APY. A penalty is imposed for early withdrawal. The APY assumes interest will remain on deposit until maturity. A withdrawal will reduce earnings. IRA Retirement CDs are only available to consumers.</p>
<p><strong>Rewards Banking with Interest Checking, Personal Interest Checking,&nbsp;Personal Money Market:</strong>&nbsp;There is no minimum balance to obtain the disclosed APY. This account is a tiered rate account. Maintenance or activity fees could reduce earnings.</p>
<p><strong>Personal Savings, Minor Savings, Holiday Saver, Coverdell Education Savings, Retirement Savings, Health Savings Account:</strong>&nbsp;There is no minimum balance to obtain the disclosed APY. Maintenance or activity fees could reduce earnings.</p>

Not available for brokered deposits, public entities, or financial institutions.</p>  </div>   <div style="width: 632px; background: #f2f2f2; border: 1px solid #cdcdcd; padding: 4px;">    <div style="margin-bottom: 4px;">     <span style="font-weight: bold; font-size: 110%;">PROMOTIONAL RELATIONSHIP RATES</span>    </div>    <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="width:100%;>" <tr=""><tbody><tr><td style="width:225px;">Term</td><td style="width:225px;">Interest Rate</td><td>Annual Percentage Yield</td></tr><tr style="font-weight: normal;"><td style="height:24px;">12-15  months</td><td>2.37%</td><td>2.40%</td></tr></tbody></table>   </div>  </div>    <br> <div style="width: 640px; margin-top: 20px;">   <p>The minimum balance to open a time deposit with a term of 90 days or more is $500. The minimum balance to open a time deposit with a term of 7-89 days is $2,500. The Relationship Pricing interest rates and APYs disclosed in this document are available to depositors who meet the following relationship requirements for the entire applicable term of the account: (i) the time deposit term must be at least 32 days, (ii) the primary or secondary designated owner on the time deposit must be the primary or secondary designated owner on a Regions Bank checking account, and (iii) the checking account must be and remain open during the entire term of the time deposit. If you do not meet the bankâ€™s relationship requirements, your account will earn the lower Standard Pricing interest rates and APYs. Details about Relationship Pricing and Standard Pricing are disclosed in other documentation related to time deposit accounts and are available from the Bankâ€™s customer service representatives. CDs (Certificates of Deposit) are time deposits. Interest on CDs longer than 12 months must be paid at least annually. Substantial penalty for early withdrawal. <h6 class="small">&nbsp;*APY=Annual Percentage Yield. APYs accurate as of 6/1/2018. Rates may change after account is opened. There is a $50 minimum balance to open account. For Kasasa Cash, if qualifications are met each monthly qualification cycle: (1) Domestic ATM fees incurred during qualification cycle will be reimbursed up to $20 ($4.99 per single transaction) and credited to account on the last day of monthly statement cycle; (2) balances up to $10,000 receive an interest rate of 2.46% with an APY of 2.50%; and (3) balances over $10,000 earn 0.51% interest rate on the portion of the balance over $10,000, resulting in 2.50% – 0.69% APY depending on the balance. If qualifications are not met on Kasasa Cash all balances earn 0.05 % APY. Qualifying transactions must post to and settle Kasasa Cash account during monthly qualification cycle. Transactions may take one or more banking days from the date transaction was made to post to and clear account. **“Monthly Qualification Cycle” means a period beginning one day prior to the first day of the current statement cycle through one day prior to the close of the current statement cycle. The advertised Kasasa Cash APY is based on compounding interest. Interest earned and ATM refunds for Kasasa Cash are automatically transferred to Kasasa Saver each statement cycle (if customer has a Kasasa Saver account). Interest does not compound. Actual interest amount paid may be less than advertised Kasasa Cash APY. The Kasasa Saver APYs may be less than Kasasa Cash APYs. If qualifications in Kasasa Cash are net each monthly qualification cycle: (1) balances up to $50,000 receive an interest rate of 1.10{% and an APY of 1.11% in Kasasa Saver (2) balances over $50,000 in Kasasa Saver earn 0.50% interest rate on portion of balance over $50,000, resulting in 1.11% -0.70% depending on the balance. If qualifications are not met on Kasasa Cash, all balances in Kasasa Saver earn 0.50% APY. Monthly direct deposit is required to have these accounts. ATM receipt must be presented for reimbursement of an individual ATM fee of $5.00 or higher. ATM processed transactions do not count towards qualifying check card transactions. To qualify for Kasasa Saver customer must have a Kasasa Cash account. Contact Us for more information about the qualification cycle. Limit one account per SSN. Fees may reduce earnings. Kasasa and Kasasa Saver are trademarks of Kasasa, Ltd., registered in the U.S.A.</h6>

                <p>
                    <sup>1</sup>
                The Annual Percentage Yield (APY) is effective as of September 27, 2018. The APY is equal to 75% of the current Upper Bound Fed Funds Target Rate. Interest rate and APY will change based on the current Upper Bound Fed Funds Target Rate. Minimum deposit of $20,000 new money required. New money is defined as monies that have not been on deposit with the S&amp;T Bank in the past thirty days. A monthly maintenance fee of $15 will be assessed if $10,000 minimum daily balance is not maintained. The account has a maximum of six (6) third party transactions permitted per month. This is a variable rate account. This account is not available for public funds. Interest rate and APY may change without prior notice. Fees may reduce earnings.
                </p>
                <p>
                    <sup>2</sup>
                This offer is not available to current S<span class="font-secondary">&amp;</span>T Bank checking customers or those who have closed an S<span class="font-secondary">&amp;</span>T Bank checking in the past 12 months. Offer applies to new consumer checking accounts (Select Banking, Preferred Banking, Preferred Banking with Interest, Four Star Banking, and Four Star Banking with Interest only) opened by 8.31.18*. New accounts will not be eligible for offer if any signer has signing authority on an existing S<span class="font-secondary">&amp;</span>T Bank consumer checking account. Signing authority will be defined by the customer name(s) and social security number(s) registered on the account. Offer cannot be combined with any other checking offer and is subject to change or termination without notice. To qualify for the first $100 offer, the new checking account must be opened with a minimum opening balance of $50 between 7.7.18 and 8.31.18 and the following conditions must be met by 9.28.18: (a) at least 10 S<span class="font-secondary">&amp;</span>T Bank Visa Debit card purchases (posted and cleared) must be made and (b) enroll in online statements. The $100 will be credited to the eligible account on 10.12.18. The additional $100 will be credited to the S<span class="font-secondary">&amp;</span>T account on or before 3.08.19 provided the account qualified for the debit card and online statement incentive. The account must remain in good standing (daily ledger balance greater than $10) in order to receive any incentive. If a $50 Refer a Friend incentive was paid out to this account during the promotional period your incentive will then be deducted by that amount. The max incentive you are able to receive during this time period is $200. Subject to 1099 reporting. 
                </p>
                <p>
                    <sup>3</sup>
                Annual Percentage Yield (APY) assumes interest remains on deposit until maturity, and withdrawal of interest will reduce earnings. CD Time Deposit - 1099 is produced in the year interest is paid. This special cannot be combined with any other offer and excludes institutional investors, brokered accounts and money for public funds. Penalty for early withdrawals could affect the APY and could reduce principal for these accounts. This CD Time Deposit APY and interest rate cannot be combined with any other promotion. Additional deposits may be made through automatic transfers from an S&amp;T checking or savings account. Minimum transfer amount is $50.  Deposits may also be made at any branch location.  Customer must have an S&amp;T checking or savings account to open the CD.  Not available on IRAs. This is a variable rate account. The APY and interest rate on the entire account balance will be adjusted and become effective the first Business Day of each month. Deposits made during the month will earn the effective rate from the date of deposit until the rate adjusts. Interest payments will only be available through transfer of funds to an S&amp;T checking or savings account. Interest will be compounded and credited quarterly on March 31, June 30, September 30 and December 31. If withdrawals are made to this account prior to maturity date, a penalty of 90 days simple interest will be imposed. The rate of interest is tied to the 91-Day Treasury Bill rate (Discount rate in effect for the last Treasury Bill auction of the previous month).

</li><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="Fully Insured with FDIC and DIF" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#fullyinsuredwithfdicanddif" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="fullyinsuredwithfdicanddif" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        Fully Insured with FDIC and DIF
    </a>
    <div class="collapse global-component-spacing-top" id="fullyinsuredwithfdicanddif">
        <div class="container">
<h3>Member FDIC and Member DIF</h3>
<p>Thanks to a combination of deposit insurance safeguards, each depositor at Salem Five Cents Savings Bank, whether using a physical branch office, salemfive.com or salemfivedirect.com, is fully insured, regardless of the number of accounts or the total funds on deposit.</p>
<p><strong>It works like this</strong>: The Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation (FDIC) now insures each depositor, for each ownership category, up to $250,000.</p>
<p>Deposits at Salem Five in excess of the standard insurance amounts provided by the FDIC are covered by the Depositors Insurance Fund (DIF). The DIF is a private, industry-sponsored insurance fund that insures all deposits above FDIC limits at Massachusetts-chartered savings banks. The DIF was established by the Massachusetts legislature in 1932 and has been insuring deposits since 1934. No depositor has ever lost a penny in a bank insured by both the FDIC and the DIF.</p>
<p><strong>The result?</strong> Your deposits at Salem Five are completely protected – without limitation.</p>
</div>
        <ul class="list-unstyled list-accordion-links gold 7613"><li class="block accordionblock   panel">

<section class="accordions global-component-spacing global-component-spacing-top" id="fdicfaqs" fdic="" dif="" faqs="">
    <div class="container">
        <div class="row">
            <div class="col-sm-12">
                    <h2>FDIC/DIF FAQs</h2>
                                        <script>
                            $(document).ready(function () {

                                setTimeout(function () {
                                    $(".2968 .accordionitemblock:first").find('.collapse').collapse('show');
                                }, 1000)
                                
                            })
                        </script>

                <ul class="list-unstyled list-accordion-links small 2968"><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="I've noticed that my bank displays the FDIC and DIF symbols. What does Member FDIC/Member DIF mean?" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#ivenoticedthatmybankdisplaysthefdicanddifsymbolswhatdoesmemberfdicmemberdifmean" aria-expanded="true" aria-controls="ivenoticedthatmybankdisplaysthefdicanddifsymbolswhatdoesmemberfdicmemberdifmean" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        I've noticed that my bank displays the FDIC and DIF symbols. What does Member FDIC/Member DIF mean?
    </a>
    <div class="collapse in" id="ivenoticedthatmybankdisplaysthefdicanddifsymbolswhatdoesmemberfdicmemberdifmean" aria-expanded="true" style="">
        <p>Salem Five is a member of both organizations that insure depositors' funds against loss. The first $250,000 per depositor is insured by the FDIC.</p>
        
    </div>
</li><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="Do all banks offer FDIC and DIF insurance coverage?" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#doallbanksofferfdicanddifinsurancecoverage" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="doallbanksofferfdicanddifinsurancecoverage" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        Do all banks offer FDIC and DIF insurance coverage?
    </a>
    <div class="collapse" id="doallbanksofferfdicanddifinsurancecoverage">
        <p>No. While there are other insuring entities, only Massachusetts-chartered savings banks offer the additional protection of DIF insurance.</p>
        
    </div>
</li><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="Are all my deposits at Salem Five insured in full?" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#areallmydepositsatsalemfiveinsuredinfull" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="areallmydepositsatsalemfiveinsuredinfull" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        Are all my deposits at Salem Five insured in full?
    </a>
    <div class="collapse" id="areallmydepositsatsalemfiveinsuredinfull">
        <p>Yes. All types of deposit accounts are covered, including savings, checking, and NOW accounts; money market accounts; certificates of deposit; IRAs and Keoghs; and all other deposit accounts held with Massachusetts-chartered savings banks.</p>
        
    </div>
</li><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="Has any depositor ever lost money in a Member FDIC/Member DIF bank?" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#hasanydepositoreverlostmoneyinamemberfdicmemberdifbank" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="hasanydepositoreverlostmoneyinamemberfdicmemberdifbank" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        Has any depositor ever lost money in a Member FDIC/Member DIF bank?
    </a>
    <div class="collapse" id="hasanydepositoreverlostmoneyinamemberfdicmemberdifbank">
        <p>No. The FDIC has always paid deposits in full up to its insurance limit. The DIF has always paid all deposits in excess of the FDIC's limit. No depositor has ever lost a penny in an FDIC/DIF member bank since either Fund was established.</p>
        
    </div>
</li><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="How financially strong are the FDIC and the DIF?" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#howfinanciallystrongarethefdicandthedif" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="howfinanciallystrongarethefdicandthedif" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        How financially strong are the FDIC and the DIF?
    </a>
    <div class="collapse" id="howfinanciallystrongarethefdicandthedif">
        <p>The FDIC is backed by the full faith and credit of the U.S. Treasury. While the DIF is not backed by federal, state, or local governments, the Fund is very strong and has extensive recourses. The banking crisis of the late 1980s serves as a poignant example of the DIF's financial strength. In this period, 18 DIF member banks failed. These banks contained funds from over 6,300 excess depositors. Their excess deposits totaled $250 million. Each and every depositor was paid in full. This was the worst period in the history of the Massachusetts thrift industry, yet the Fund has more money today than it did at the start of the crisis.</p>
        
    </div>
</li><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="Is the DIF subject to any form of regulatory scrutiny?" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#isthedifsubjecttoanyformofregulatoryscrutiny" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="isthedifsubjecttoanyformofregulatoryscrutiny" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        Is the DIF subject to any form of regulatory scrutiny?
    </a>
    <div class="collapse" id="isthedifsubjecttoanyformofregulatoryscrutiny">
        <p>Yes. The DIF's financial records are examined regularly by the Massachusetts Commissioner of Banks, and audited annually by an independent auditor.</p>
        
    </div>
</li><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="If a Member FDIC/Member DIF bank ever got into financial trouble, how would I get my money?" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#ifamemberfdicmemberdifbankevergotintofinancialtroublehowwouldigetmymoney" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="ifamemberfdicmemberdifbankevergotintofinancialtroublehowwouldigetmymoney" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        If a Member FDIC/Member DIF bank ever got into financial trouble, how would I get my money?
    </a>
    <div class="collapse" id="ifamemberfdicmemberdifbankevergotintofinancialtroublehowwouldigetmymoney">
        <p>Based on past experience, arrangements would be made for all deposits to be automatically transferred to another bank. All your deposit funds would be available with no interruption of service.</p>
        
    </div>
</li><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="I'd like to buy a CD for $325,000. Is it fully insured if I place it in one account, or will I need to open two accounts in different names?" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#idliketobuyacdfor325000isitfullyinsuredifiplaceitinoneaccountorwillineedtoopentwoaccountsindifferentnames" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="idliketobuyacdfor325000isitfullyinsuredifiplaceitinoneaccountorwillineedtoopentwoaccountsindifferentnames" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        I'd like to buy a CD for $325,000. Is it fully insured if I place it in one account, or will I need to open two accounts in different names?
    </a>
    <div class="collapse" id="idliketobuyacdfor325000isitfullyinsuredifiplaceitinoneaccountorwillineedtoopentwoaccountsindifferentnames">
        <p>You can buy a single CD for the entire amount. At a Member FDIC/Member DIF member bank, your deposits are fully insured, even if they exceed $250,000.</p>
        
    </div>
</li><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="Does the FDIC or the DIF insure investments in bank mutual funds?" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#doesthefdicorthedifinsureinvestmentsinbankmutualfunds" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="doesthefdicorthedifinsureinvestmentsinbankmutualfunds" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        Does the FDIC or the DIF insure investments in bank mutual funds?
    </a>
    <div class="collapse" id="doesthefdicorthedifinsureinvestmentsinbankmutualfunds">
        <p>No. Both the FDIC and DIF only cover deposits.</p>
        
    </div>
</li><li class="block accordionitemblock   panel">
    <a title="Where can I learn more about the FDIC and DIF?" class="accordion-header" data-toggle="collapse" href="#wherecanilearnmoreaboutthefdicanddif" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="wherecanilearnmoreaboutthefdicanddif" data-parent="#accordion-grp-1">
        Where can I learn more about the FDIC and DIF?
    </a>
    <div class="collapse" id="wherecanilearnmoreaboutthefdicanddif">
        <p>Visit the <a title="FDIC" href="https://www.fdic.gov/consumers/consumer/news/index.html" target="_blank">FDIC</a> and <a title="DIF" href="https://www.difxs.com/DIF/Home.aspx" target="_blank">DIF</a> websites where you can access additional information. </p>
        
    </div>
</li></ul>
            </div>
            
        </div>
    </div>
</section>
